Germans Eagerly Donate Books 40

To Help Rebuild the Oriental Library

Two Thousand Volumes to be Shipped to Shanghai Soon

(Berlin) In order to help China restore the Shanghai Zhabei Oriental Library, which was destroyed by Japanese troops during the January 28th Incident, the Emergency Joint Association organized by German scientists has collected more than 2,000 volumes of great German literary works, which are scheduled to be shipped to Shanghai within the next week. This move was initiated by many members of the Sino-German Friendship Association of Frankfurt in Germany who are traveling in Shanghai, and German libraries, publishing houses, and the scientific community and individuals have enthusiastically supported it. The collected books are related to the most advanced standard works of German science and culture. The goal is to enable Chinese people and scholars to understand German art and thought. In addition, there are many valuable books on the study of German architecture and the description of German scenery. The Oriental Library

originally had a complete set of Liebich's Yearbook of Chemistry and Pharmacology, from 1821 to 1930, which was also destroyed by artillery fire, which is a great pity. This book is now rare. A part of it has been found by members of the Friendship Association and shipped to Shanghai, and it is hoped that the remaining missing volumes can be gradually found from the hands of various private collectors. Furthermore, the German Farben Trust provided particularly strong support for this move and contributed a large sum of money when purchasing this chemical yearbook. The books can be shipped to Shanghai around the end of March, and according to the latest news, those in all circles in Germany who care about Chinese culture and friendship will continue to work on this throughout the year. This move by Germany is truly a model for other countries. (2nd National Telegram)

Trial of the Box Corpse Case Continues 41

(Dalian) The trial of the box corpse case continued today. Nakazono also claimed that Dr. Kodama had begun to wrestle Aoyagi, and then he joined the fight, and in his anger, he stabbed his enemy. The court tried to force Dr. Kodama to come here from Japan to testify, but today

the doctor examined his body and said that he was weak and unable to travel. (3rd Reuters Telegram)

Significant Success of US Monetary Policy 42

London Gold Prices Soar Continuously

Domestic Prices Expected to Rise

Preliminary Anglo-American Negotiations Underway

(Washington) According to important US government personnel, the new monetary policy of the United States has already achieved significant success. The sudden increase in gold prices in London, England, shows that the price increases desired by the United States can also rise accordingly, proving that the United States can indeed manipulate global gold and commodity prices. Currently, the $2,000,000,000 stabilization exchange fund has not been fully utilized, and will likely wait until the planned price of $35 per ounce of gold can be implemented. According to financial circles, the new US monetary policy has caused no harm to the economic organizations of various countries. On the contrary, higher prices would benefit all countries. As for the devaluation of the US dollar, it is said to be intended to absorb foreign gold. (2nd, National Dispatch)

Establishment of a National Bank to Encourage Export Trade 43

(Washington) Today, President Roosevelt and Jesse Jones, Chairman of the Reconstruction Finance Corporation, announced the decision to establish a National Trade Bank, specializing in assisting trade with Russia and other countries. This bank (or corporation) will have full authority to assist importers and exporters, and can provide loans or guarantees for mortgages, etc. Jones stated that the primary purpose of the National Trade Bank is to promote trade with Russia, but it will also provide assistance to import and export activities with other countries. The bank is planned to be located in Washington, D.C., as it is subordinate to the Reconstruction Finance Corporation. As for the amount of capital, Jones said it has not yet been estimated, but will be approximately similar to the $400 million capital of the Commodity Credit Corporation. It is reported that the President had previously discussed this matter in detail with Jones and US Ambassador to Russia, William Bullitt. (2nd, National Dispatch)

No Intention to Conclude International Monetary Agreement at Present 44

(Washington) White House officials stated that the US government currently has no intention of concluding an international monetary agreement. (2nd, Havas Dispatch)

(Paris) French officials indicate that President Roosevelt's decision regarding the price of the dollar is a sign that the United States is gradually joining countries that use gold. It is believed that this is a step towards global cooperation and exchange policies, and to stabilize the dollar. (2nd, Reuters)

(Washington) Tentative and informal Anglo-American monetary discussions are currently underway, handled by diplomatic authorities from both sides or the Bank of England and the New York Federal Reserve Bank, as a preliminary step to formal negotiations. According to commercial reports, these talks aim to prevent a currency war, which would force France to abandon the gold standard. It is hoped that both sides can establish a temporary currency truce and use their equalization funds to seek exchange rate stability and avoid large-scale US gold trading abroad. Although the US capital advocates temporarily setting one pound equal to five US dollars, officials today clarified that no fixed ratio has been requested. Officials also acknowledge that Britain enjoys a special advantage in controlling the pound because the pound is not bound by gold. At the same time, the inflow of gold into the United States is only limited by shipping convenience, and gold worth over $30 million is currently awaiting shipment. Wall Street in New York indicates that yesterday's variable movements of the US dollar were due to the repatriation of US funds and the influx of foreign funds from France and elsewhere. (3rd, Reuters)

Utilizing New Price Advantages to Acquire Foreign Gold 45

(New York) According to today's news, New York banks are now taking advantage of the new gold prices to buy gold and have already received cash worth $11 million from abroad, which will be shipped to the United States. (2nd, Reuters)

Large Amounts of Gold Discovered in the Rocky Mountain Area of the United States 46

Denver: Recently, large amounts of placer gold have been discovered in the gold mines of the Rocky Mountain area near Denver. The local mint has received a total of 84,350,673 ounces of placer gold in recent days, compared to only 79,471,895 ounces received in January last year. According to mining experts in the Rocky Mountain area, 1939 will be the best year for harvests. The government is now planning to increase gold and silver prices, so gold mining operations are becoming more active. (2nd, National Dispatch)

Japan Plans to Permanently Occupy South Pacific Mandated Islands 47

Hirota States to British Reporter

(London) The London Daily Express today carried a Tokyo dispatch stating that the newspaper's reporter recently met with Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota. In the conversation, Hirota declared that the former German Pacific islands, currently mandated to Japan by the League of Nations, would never be returned to the League of Nations under any circumstances. Hirota further stated that during the European War, the Allied Powers concluded a secret treaty with Japan, allowing Japan to receive land as compensation. Therefore, these former German islands should be ceded to Japan. The mandated procedure was merely a strategy to avoid President Wilson's opposition. Hirota concluded that the rights to govern these naval bases, which are of great military importance, are based on what can be called permanent jurisdiction, and that this permanent jurisdiction does not depend on the League of Nations. (2nd, National Dispatch)

Huang Shaoxiong Discusses the Registration Process of the China International Famine Relief Commission 58

(Nanjing) Minister of the Interior Huang Shaoxiong made a statement on the issue of the China International Famine Relief Commission's registration, saying that he has always attached great importance to the undertakings of the commission. Since the promulgation of the regulations on the registration of charitable organizations, the commission has not completed the registration in accordance with the statutory procedures. After repeated urging, in order to determine its legal person status, it was submitted to the Beiping Municipal Government for transmittal to the Ministry for registration in January of this year, and requested that the Ministry be the direct supervisory body of the commission. This has been approved by the Ministry and submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval. The so-called direct supervision refers only to the general commission. The branch commissions in various places should still be handled by the competent authorities in accordance with regulations. Now that the general commission is under the direct supervision of the Ministry, it will do its best to promote its development, and plans to send personnel to inspect it in the near future. It is deeply hoped that the commission will continue its past spirit and make greater progress, especially in completing the registration items and submitting them to the Ministry for approval in the near future. Improving Measures to Block Salt in Bandit Areas 68

(Nanjing) Regarding measures to block salt in bandit areas, the Ministry of Finance stated that the salt public sales bureau was originally organized by military agencies. However, as salt tax revenue was greatly affected, Yao Yuanlun was commissioned to visit Jiang Jieshi in Jiangxi for instructions. Jiang then approved four improved measures: 1. In provinces with management bureaus, in addition to the original deputy director, an additional deputy director should be added to assist the director in handling salt public sales. The director of the provincial salt transport bureau will concurrently serve. 2. In counties with public sales committees and branch committees, where there are salt affairs agencies, the person in charge of the salt affairs agency will participate as a member of the committee. In places without salt affairs agencies, the salt transport bureau will send personnel to participate as members of the public sales committee. 3. In accordance with the provisions of Articles 6 and 24 of the public sales regulations, in addition to reporting to the provincial finance department, security department, and management bureau, the salt transport bureau should also be notified. 4. All those who should apply for a permit from the salt affairs agency but do not, will be regarded as private salt and will be handled by the salt affairs agency in accordance with regulations. Those who violate the blockade regulations will be handled by the management bureau in accordance with the blockade regulations, but the confiscated salt should still be handed over to the local public sales committee for sale and should not be transported to other places for sale. (3rd, Special Dispatch)

Parliamentary Struggle in Japan (Japanese Dispatch) 94

Conflict Between Military Cliques and Zaibatsu

The issue of military discipline has escalated from simmering tensions to open confrontation. Originally, within Japan, since the September 18th Shenyang Incident, all major domestic decisions have been made by the military, especially the army. Firstly, they had all made great contributions; secondly, the policies implemented by the military seemed effective. Therefore, the entire Japanese people focused their attention on military actions, believing that the inherent problems of Japan would be solved along with the expansion of territories. Contrary to expectations, occupying Manchuria, in the general Japanese ideal, was supposed to alleviate Japan’s economic difficulties, but in reality, besides expanding the military budget and increasing military industry, there were no other achievements. The general rural areas continued to suffer and bear heavier tax burdens. Regarding the benefits of immigration, the current puppet state (Manchuria) has only placed about two thousand Japanese officials, which has little impact on the unemployment problem of Japanese intellectuals. The armed immigration, which was vigorously promoted in rural areas, has only relocated about one thousand five hundred people to Jilin and Jiamusi in the past two years. It cannot be said to have alleviated the economic panic in rural areas. Therefore, the credibility of the military has gradually declined. However, because there are veterans' associations and various right-wing groups there to support the military, and with power as backing, although the people are full of dissatisfaction, no one dares to say a word. Newspapers cannot express any dissatisfaction. But before this session of the 65th Diet convened, there were various brewing, namely brewing a general attack on the military cliques. First, the zaibatsu took the opportunity to counterattack the military cliques. For more than two years, no one dared to criticize the Japanese military cliques, because they had made great achievements and had great power, so no one dared to say what shortcomings there were in the military's policy of invading China. Big and small bureaucrats had to follow the orders of the military. Although the zaibatsu were the main force in parliamentary politics, when military power was above everything else, they had no choice but to obey the military cliques. Therefore, no one dared to say anything about the assassinations of Junnosuke Inoue and Takuma Dan, nor dared to criticize Japan's security problems. Even Prime Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi, who was in office, was shot and killed by a dozen active-duty army and navy officers who broke into the official residence in broad daylight. No one dared to raise questions of responsibility. More than a year later, Seiyukai member Yutaka Miyazawa formally questioned the impropriety of punishing the army and navy murderers in the House of Representatives, daring to criticize it head-on. This is a fact rarely seen in a country ruled by law. However, Japan has never completely broken away from feudal relations, and when military cliques are rampant, the majority party in the Diet is also useless. Now that the military's weakness has been exposed, even those who support the military have adopted a spectator attitude. The general public is deeply dissatisfied with the actions of the military cliques, so the zaibatsu took the opportunity to rise up, wanting to frustrate the power of the military and restore the power of financial capital. Second, the issue of military discipline. In a militaristic country, military unity should be unquestionable. How could one know that within the Japanese military, the veteran faction and the young and middle-aged faction had different views on gradual and steady progress versus rapid and forceful action? Recently, this tendency has become clearer, both towards the Soviet Union and the United States. Now the people in the general class, such as Araki, also know that Japan cannot fight abroad now, because its economic power is weak. However, people below the rank of lieutenant colonel still advocate launching a war quickly. Therefore, recently, the general literary world in Japan is almost covered with publications that advocate war and promote extraordinary times. Therefore, the zaibatsu have now formally proposed in the Diet to ban books that advocate war. This is also one aspect of the struggle between the military and the zaibatsu. Third, the issue of ideology. In Japan, this divine country, dangerous thoughts breed exceptionally quickly. It is understandable that the people and farmers are seriously affected in their lives. It can also be explained that intellectuals such as the daughter of Hajime Kawakami are influenced by academic theories. Only the son of Zenjiro Shibata, the former cabinet secretary-general, has become a communist. Recently, the sister of Duke Iwakura Tomosada, the younger brother of Viscount Ogura Sueyoshi, the eldest son of Viscount Mori Toshinari, and the second son of Viscount Hachijo Takamasa are all active participants in the red underground movement. Moreover, it is said that there are forty or fifty students of the aristocracy in Gakushuin who have been infected by communism. These are all reactions to the military's policy of aggression, and they are also powerful weapons to attack the current government. Therefore, military men have to retreat temporarily. Although parliamentary politics may not necessarily rise, military dictatorship is not easy to realize temporarily. (Tokyo, January 28, 1934)

First Phase of Bandit Suppression in Sichuan Completed 95

| Liu Xiang Talks About Bandit Suppression, Rehabilitation, and Advancement |

Chengdu Correspondence: Sichuan's military campaign to suppress bandits, since the 1st Route cleared bandits in Zhaohua, Guangyuan, and Jian'ge; the 2nd Route cleared bandits along the Langzhong-Ba Road; the 3rd and 4th Routes cleared bandits in Yingjing and Peng'an; the 2nd and 3rd Routes cleared bandits in Yilong; and the 5th Route cleared bandits in Xuanhan and Sui County, the first phase of the bandit suppression plan was completely completed, and it rapidly transitioned to the second phase. This was in mid-January. After January 17th, Wang Lingji, Commander-in-Chief of the 5th Route, and Fan Shaozeng, Deputy Commander-in-Chief, learned that the bandit Xu's ammunition had been exhausted, so they led their troops to climb vines and brave the snow, taking advantage of the situation to advance rapidly. On the 23rd, they captured Madu Pass, the only natural barrier between Suixuan, Tongjiang, and Bazhong. Because the bandits lost their barrier to Tongjiang and Bazhong, their momentum was greatly diminished, and they were on the verge of annihilation, retreating a hundred miles a day. The reporter, believing that the Sichuan situation had transitioned from a period of full-force bandit suppression to a period of simultaneous bandit suppression and rehabilitation, visited Liu Xiang yesterday to inquire about his usual methods for carrying out the three points of bandit suppression, rehabilitation, and development. Liu Xiang replied as follows: (I (Liu referring to himself) have been entrusted by the Central Government with the dual responsibilities of bandit suppression and rehabilitation. Knowing my own inadequacy and inability to bear such a heavy burden, I have been conscientious and self-disciplined day and night. For the past six months, fortunately, all parties have cooperated and devoted their efforts to suppressing bandits. Seeing the successive recapture of Xuanhan, Sui County, Yingjing, and Yilong, the remnants of bandits in Zhaohua, Guangyuan, Jian'ge, Langzhong, Cangxi, Nanbu, and Peng'an counties have also been gradually eliminated. The bandits' momentum has been greatly diminished, and we are currently formulating a second step encirclement plan to completely eliminate them between Tongjiang, Nanjiang, and Bazhong, preventing them from fleeing and causing further harm to neighboring provinces. As for the current rehabilitation strategies, we are leading the entire Sichuan military and civilians to present their abilities and talents and make the best use of them to engage in development. We must break the past situation of horizontal and vertical divisions and armed coercion and transition to competition in business, making the best use of everyone's abilities and the land, so that everyone has a job and helps each other in governance. Recently, our army has been striving to reduce its size, reducing two soldiers per squad, and has successively discharged more than 20,000 officers and soldiers, intending to show consideration for the people's strength and establish a standard first, not to restrict all armies to reduce their size. As for the overall plan, it will only be possible to implement it when everyone has a job. Currently, it is hoped that all armies can unanimously influence each other, reduce their size on their own, and strive to achieve a balance between income and expenditure. However, there is absolutely no intention of requesting or restricting other armies to follow suit. Furthermore, rumors that the Sichuan army has been reorganized into three armies and that the governor's office has established several departments are also not true. Because during this period of bandit suppression and rehabilitation, all provincial government matters and war powers of the governor's office will only be handled in accordance with the instructions of the Central Government. There are no preconceived notions or any decisions. I personally only know to obey the orders of the Central Government and fulfill my duties. Everything else is beyond my concern. At this critical time of urgent foreign and domestic troubles, there is no other way to survive except to work hard, be pragmatic, and lead by example." (National News Agency)

Supreme Court's Order for the Arrest of Li Zongtong 96

| Li Suspected of Being Involved in the Palace Museum Embezzlement Case |

The Supreme Court Procuratorate instructed the chief prosecutors of the high courts of all provinces, stating: The case of Yi Peiji, the former director of the Peiping Palace Museum, embezzling funds during his tenure, in addition to the part that has already been investigated and prosecuted by the Jiangning District Court Procuratorate, the remaining part is still under investigation. Li Zongtong, the former secretary-general of the museum, is also suspected of embezzlement. He has been summoned by the Jiangning District Court Procuratorate multiple times, and summons have been served by public announcement, but he has not yet appeared in court. The procuratorate has reported the situation to this office and successively instructed the chief prosecutors of the Shanghai, Peiping, and Tianjin courts to separately detain him. It is now found that Li Zongtong is hiding without a trace and cannot be detained. In accordance with Articles 50 and 51 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a warrant is hereby issued, instructing the chief prosecutor to comply and instruct his subordinates to comply, strictly arrest him, and bring him to justice. This order is hereby issued, with one warrant attached. February 1, 23rd year of the Republic of China, Prosecutor-General Zheng Lie.

The First Department of the Nanchang Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission announces one of the ironclad proofs of the Fujian rebel army's alliance with the Red bandits, recorded as follows: According to personnel who previously served in the rebel 61st Division, they carried an order issued by the rebel division in Quanzhou at 10:10 AM on December 28th. The first item stated that our friendly forces were concentrated in Tai'ning and were attacking the enemy's right flank towards Shunchang and Jian'ou. The second item stated that our First Front Army was gathering forces in Fuzhou to lure the enemy deep, etc. The so-called "Our First Front Army" refers to the entire rebel army of the former 19th Route Army. The so-called "Our friendly forces" refers to the Red bandits. This is evidenced by the fact that the main force of the rebel army is currently concentrated near Fuzhou, and the main force of the Jiangxi Red bandits is gathering in Jian'ning, Tai'ning, and Xiamao, etc., which coincides with the order mentioned by the rebels. A mimeographed copy of the order issued by the rebel division commander Liang Shiji is hereby printed and announced to the people of the country to clarify the crime of the rebels' alliance with the Red bandits to endanger our party and country. First Department of the Nanchang Headquarters of the Military Affairs Commission.

19th Route Army in Quanzhou Obeys Reorganization and Disbandment 98

= Cai Tingkai's Situation When He Was Defeated and Fled =

= 19th Route Army Obeys Orders to Leave Quanzhou and Await Reorganization =

Xiamen Correspondence: When the 19th Route Army was in Fuzhou, Cai Tingkai still wanted to combine the main forces of the Shen District and Mao's various units to fight a decisive battle with the Central Army at Shuikou and Gutian. However, when Cai led the army to Shuikou, there was not a single soldier there. At this point, he realized that the strategy had failed and knew that the Central Army in Yanping and Shuikou had already crossed the river and was heading to Youxi, going south towards Yongtai and Xianyou, encircling the retreat route in southern Fujian. Cai then ordered the abandonment of Fuzhou and a general retreat towards southern Fujian. They did not dare to stay in Minqing and Fuqing along the way. Xianyou was already occupied by the 10th Division of the Central Army, and the 83rd Division had also encircled Baoling in northern Hui'an, cutting off the rear route. Cai himself was in Putian at that time, commanding the entire army, hoping to defend Putian and Xianyou to the death. Later, the rear route Futuling was cut off, and Cai was also surrounded. Therefore, Li Jinsheng, the head of Cai's special service regiment, personally led three companies to charge Wangling fiercely. Cai followed in a car, breaking through the encirclement. He had only a few dozen people left in Hui'an. When Cai's car broke through, the horse grooms and others in the car were destroyed, and all the guards died. It was almost a miracle that Cai was not captured. This was at noon on January 20th. As for the retreating soldiers, they still fought fiercely with the Central Army at Tuling and Kandou on the morning of the 21st and then retreated to Huian for a short rest, then retreated to Quanzhou. Wei Lihuang captured Huixian County on the afternoon of the 21st, and the vanguard arrived at Luoyang Bridge that night. The 19th Route Army was south of Luoyang Bridge, facing the Central Army across the bridge. Cai and others arrived in Quanzhou on the evening of the 20th and stayed at Mao Weisou's residence in Yuqun Lane. Soon they learned that the generals had the intention of defecting and that the situation could not be salvaged, so they expressed their intention to leave. That night, Shen and Mao held a farewell banquet. During the banquet, they looked at each other sadly. On the morning of the 21st, Cai took a car with a secretary and dozens of guards, bidding farewell to the south. On the verge of departure, he still urged them to preserve their strength and retreat. At 10:00 AM, he arrived in Zhangzhou. At that time, the 19th Route Army in Zhangzhou had already retreated completely. He then followed the last sentry westward to Longyan. After Cai left, the division commanders promoted Mao Weisou to be the temporary commander of the entire army. On one hand, they sent Zhao Jinwen, the staff officer of the 61st Division, to Luoyang Town alone to bring a letter to Wei Lihuang, explaining that the 19th Route Army had all defected and would await the Central Government's handling. Please do not attack again to avoid sacrifices on both sides. Wei, because he had not yet received the Central Government's orders, telegraphed Chiang Ting-wen for instructions. Chiang Ting-wen had just received a telegram from Chairman Chiang, so he replied to stop the attack. Wei then immediately agreed to a ceasefire. That day, Chiang Ting-wen sent an adjutant to Luoyang to convey Chairman Chiang's telegram. The adjutant also went to Quanzhou in the same car with the commander of the 83rd Division to meet Mao. Also coming were the chief of staff of the 83rd Division and two regimental commanders. Mao and Shen hosted a banquet for them and returned to Luoyang that night. When the 19th Route Army defected, the Central Government's telegram ordered: (1) Designate locations for separate assembly and await the Central Government's personnel for reorganization; (2) The 60th Division is designated to assemble at Yuzhen in Fuqing, the 61st Division at Tuling and Kantou in Huian, the 78th Division at Hanjiang in Putian, the 49th Division at Fengting in Xianyou, and Qiu Zhaochen's unit at Jiangkou; (3) Reorganization method: officers and soldiers below the rank of battalion commander can choose to stay and await reorganization or surrender their weapons, receive gratuities, and be sent back to their hometowns. The appointment and dismissal of senior officers above the rank of battalion commander are subject to the Central Government's orders; (4) Comply with the orders and leave Quanzhou completely before the 25th, and depart to the designated locations. After Wei Lihuang contacted Mao Weisou and others, the result was that Mao and others were willing to comply with the orders. At about 4:00 AM on the 25th, the troops in Quanzhou began to leave Quanzhou, passing through the Central Army's position at Luoyang Bridge through the east gate and heading towards Huian, Putian, Fuqing, Xianyou, and other places. The 19th Route Army troops originally stationed in Shashi, Qingyuan, Honglai, Anhai, Guanqiao, and Xiwei had all retreated to Quanzhou first and departed together. By 2:00 PM on the 25th, the joint office of the four divisions of the 19th Route Army in Quanzhou had also withdrawn from the city. The entire withdrawal was completed by about 5:00 PM. Only one battalion of Pang Chenggen's 61st Division was stationed in Quanzhou to maintain order. At about 8:00 PM that night, Chen Peiyu's unit of Chen Guohui's remnants and Huang Yuxi and others entered the city from the south gate. Peng Tang entered the city from the west gate. Peng surrendered dozens of weapons from the Public Security Bureau and then withdrew from the city. Chen fought fiercely with the sentries of the 19th Route Army on South Street. Chen's unit was defeated and had a hundred weapons confiscated, including more than forty Mauser pistols and more than eighty rifles. Chen's unit originally came to seize weapons, truly "trying to steal a chicken but losing rice instead." At 10:00 PM, the 10th Division of Wei Lihuang's unit entered the city from Luoyang Bridge. They heard fierce street fighting in the city and knew that it was militia coming to seize weapons. Therefore, they joined forces with the 19th Route Army to confiscate Chen's unit's weapons and disperse more than a hundred militiamen. On the morning of the 26th, the last troops of the 19th Route Army retreated completely. The 10th Division immediately announced a curfew throughout the city, prohibiting militia from entering the city. The Fifth Route Command of Wei Lihuang also moved from Luoyang Bridge to the old government office on Hui Street in Quanzhou. The 10th Division and the 83rd Division successively entered the city that day. Wei Lihuang also entered Quanzhou at noon. Chiang Ting-wen went to Tong'an from Xiamen on the 25th to command the 3rd Division to advance to Shuitou. The 89th Division took over the defense of Xiwei, Guanqiao, and Anhai. They also entered Quanzhou by car from Tong'an in the afternoon of the 26th, staying at the Lianhuan Society with Wei. The 89th Division entered Quanzhou on the 27th. Division Commander Tang Enbo also arrived. The unit was stationed in Honglai. There are currently three divisions in Quanzhou: the 10th, 93rd, and 89th. After the 19th Route Army departed, Mao Weisou, Ou Shounian, Shen Guanghan, and Zhang Yan all followed the army. Only Tan Qixiu was eliminated. The four divisions of Shen and Mao, in addition to the parts that were eliminated in Baisha, Huian, and Putian, still have a total strength of 30,000 men gathering in various places in compliance with orders. Mao and Zhang returned to Quanzhou from Huian on the 27th to negotiate reorganization matters with Chiang Ting-wen and Wei Lihuang. However, although the 19th Route Army still has a strength of 30,000 men, this time they are gathering separately in various places, all in areas crowded with the Central Army. Their strength has already been dispersed, making it easy to reorganize and disband them. Chiang Ting-wen flew to Fuzhou again from Quanzhou on the 28th. The military affairs in southern Fujian have come to an end here. (January 29th)

Songjiang - Fishing Boat Robbed Mid-Journey 99

Shanghai Yongji Fish Firm recently transported a large batch of grass carp to Qingpu for sale to meet the needs of the New Year. However, when the boat arrived at Desheng Port, the tide fell and it ran aground, mooring there to wait for the tide to depart. Then a pirate ship from that place came forward to rob, loading the fish and fleeing. The firm's owner, Ling Anhuai, tracked them to Songjiang and reported to the Third Precinct. Inspector Gu led the police to investigate the beach area of Cangqiao, where they found a fishing boat. They summoned the owner to identify it, who confirmed the person who robbed the fish. The suspect, Zhang Jinsheng, was arrested and confessed without hesitation. The stolen goods have been sent to the Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Suzhou - Construction of the Suzhou-Changzhou Highway Begins 100

The Changzhou section of the Suzhou-Changzhou Highway has already been completed.

However, the Suzhou section has been suspended due to successive floods and wars. Now, due to the frequent urging of the provincial authorities to start construction, the county government has scheduled technicians Jiang Kuibing and Hua Chi to lead workers and laborers to carry out surveying tomorrow (the 5th). The project is planned to start from outside Qimen to Wuta, and construction is scheduled to begin in late this month.

Large Number of Businesses Close in Suzhou 101

The Suzhou business community has been affected by the current situation, and the market is declining day by day. Many businesses have closed in recent days due to economic turnover problems. Yesterday (the 3rd), Huafeng Sauce Garden on Lindun Road also closed, losing more than 20,000 gold. Hutou Yuantaiyi Rice Store and Yuanfengyi Rice Store have also closed one after another. Yuantaiyi lost 40,000 gold. Yuanfengyi closed due to the impact of Yuantaiyi. It is expected that by the end of the lunar year, there may be a large number of stores announcing their closure.

Rickshaw Pullers Staged a Strike at the Train Station 102

Yesterday (the 3rd) at 9:45 AM, when a Shanghai passenger train arrived in Suzhou, a rickshaw puller named Xia A Da was picking up passengers at the station. Liu Yao and other officers of the station police section interfered because he violated the regulations, hitting Xia A Da on the head. This triggered a reaction from the rickshaw pullers. About two hundred rickshaws staged a full strike and prevented horse-drawn carriages from picking up passengers at the station. The situation was very tense. Stationmaster Zhuang and others went to the rickshaw pullers' union and invited Chairman Li Jingcheng and Standing Committee member Lu Yiwan to mediate. The situation was restored to normal at 5:00 PM.

Since the arrest and execution of the bandit Stone Pond Younger Brother in this county, the banditry temporarily subsided. The night before yesterday, they looted the Yangjiabang area, causing residents there to suffer considerable losses. While they were reporting to the county to request arrest, the Wang family, a farmer in Xiaowan, North Bamboo, Xitang, was kidnapped. It is said that it was also done by the same gang of bandits. As a result, store account boats are afraid to move forward. Bandits are everywhere, making people afraid to talk about tigers.

A type of Red Scarf Bandit has now been discovered in the county's northern countryside, with red cloth wrapped around their heads as a symbol, and they are exceptionally fierce. Yesterday, in the Dongzhi Township area of the Fourth District, seven or eight Red Scarf Bandits suddenly arrived, coming from Qianmu Dang, and robbed seven homes, including Yu Dongshan, Yu Xuchu, and Sun Liuting. All their money, belongings, clothing, and bedding were robbed. The county prison has recently been involved in various dark secrets, such as the chief guard beating

and injuring prisoners and the sale of red pills inside the prison. The evidence is conclusive. Since January, as many as seven prisoners have died in a row. It is said that most of the allegations made by the Education Association are true.

Wuxi - Agricultural Bank Handles Agricultural Product Sales 106

The Farmers Bank, in order to facilitate the cooperative societies or farmers in various places to transport and sell agricultural products, has specially established an agricultural product sales office in Shanghai. Its business includes: (1) acting as an agent for cooperative societies or farmers to transport and sell agricultural products; (2) acting as an agent for cooperative societies or farmers to purchase fertilizers and seeds; (3) providing member cooperative societies with market information. The articles of association have been sent to the Construction Department for separate distribution. All purchases and sales by cooperative societies or farmers will be handled by the agricultural product sales office. A special letter was sent to the cooperative organizations yesterday for reference.

Rice and Bean Industry Changes Commission 107

The Rice, Bean, and Miscellaneous Grain Trade Association of this county previously reduced the commission of 1% (one cent per dollar) deducted for buying and selling on behalf of customers due to the drastic drop in the market price of rice and grain over the years. However, various expenses have become increasingly heavy and difficult to maintain. Therefore, it was decided that from July 1st of last year, the commission would be changed to 0.16%. It is now learned that the Wujin trade association also feels that the original 1% commission is insufficient to cover expenses. It has consulted with the trade association of this county back and forth and decided to uniformly follow the example of this county and change it to 0.16%. It will be implemented from February 18th of this year.

Yu Liankui, the director of the Wuyi Detention Center, said that most of the detainees were cases sent by the county government, either bandits or thieves. They were all afraid of being punished severely during the strict campaign to eliminate bandits. Therefore, they were arrogant and domineering, breaking the regulations of the center. Even for minor matters, they would gather and shout. Recently, they even intended to cause trouble in the prison and could not be reformed, especially Zhang Shuda and Wang Mingzhang. Yesterday, he specially requested instructions from the county government. County Magistrate Cai instructed that the two prisoners were indeed extremely illegal and should be transferred to prison for custody pending investigation.

Yangzhou Ministry of Finance Approval Regarding the Northern Relocation of Huai River Transportation 109

Previously, people from this county, deeply concerned about the impact on the Huainan market due to Lianghuai Transport Commissioner Miao Qiujie's proposal to abolish the administrative power of the Huainan Deputy Transport Commissioner and relocate transport merchants northward, requested Wang Boling, a member of the Central Committee, to directly telegraph Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance to take measures to prevent it. The Ministry of Finance immediately replied, agreeing to discuss the matter at length. Furthermore, Hu Zhen, Bao Xiangzhong, and others submitted petitions to various departments, provinces, and counties, appealing to prevent the decline of the Yangzhou market. Now, it is heard that the Ministry of Finance still insists on collecting taxes and releasing salt in Yangzhou. However, administrative matters concerning the distribution of salt permits must be unified under the Transport Commissioner. This Ministry, in order to reorganize Lianghuai transport affairs and unify authority, has already approved the management of salt permit distribution in the Xiang, E, West Anhui, and West Anhui areas by the Lianghuai Transport Commissioner. This measure only slightly modifies the merchants' reporting procedures. Tax collection and salt release for sail-transported goods will continue to be managed by the Yangzhou Audit Sub-Office, concurrently handled by the Huainan Deputy Transport Commissioner, which will not affect the Yangzhou market or finance. The petition appears to be a misunderstanding. It is hereby approved for your information.)

Zhenjiang Jiangsu Provincial Government Plans to Rescue Rural Areas 110

In recent years, rural areas have been on the verge of bankruptcy, and the economic panic has reached its peak. The reason is nothing more than low grain prices harming farmers. Currently, the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the Department of Finance are actively planning to rescue rural areas. Since the commencement of this work, it has been decided to first organize agricultural warehouse management committees in Zhenjiang, Gaoyou, Jiangdu, and other counties, temporarily collecting four types of food grains: rice, wheat, paddy, and beans, according to market prices and storing them in the warehouses of each county. The purpose is to stabilize market prices and circulate rural finance, so that farmers will not lament "no one wants to exchange goods for money." It is heard that the personnel for the agricultural warehouse management committees in the three counties are all appointed by the Department of Finance, including local county magistrates and bankers, etc. They were dispatched a few days ago, carrying cash, to various villages to purchase grain, slightly raising the price per dan (unit of weight) according to local market prices. Since the commencement of purchases, farmers have been enthusiastically selling accumulated grain. In addition, the influx of large amounts of cash into the countryside has gradually activated financial turnover, which is widely praised as convenient.

Nantong Impersonating Education Committee Member to Defraud Money Arrested 111

The Education Bureau has arrested Feng Dewei, who impersonated a member of the Education Committee and extorted money from private schools in various districts under the pretext of registration. Those who were defrauded of money amounted to more than 300 cases. He was taken to the county government on the 2nd.

Qingjiang Four Members of a Family Tragically Murdered in Revenge 112

In the Xiaowuji area, bordering Siyang County, northwest of Yugou Town in the Fourth District of Huaiyin, a villager named Lin Yucheng's son, Zongmei, had served as a soldier in the supplementary regiments of the 25th and 1st Route Armies, and also served as a detective in the county police brigade. He had successively arrested bandits Chen Weigang, Liu Si, and Liu Qicai, all of whom had been executed. As a result, he incurred deep resentment from the bandits. On the evening of the 29th of the month, the bandits gathered a gang of more than ten people and went to his house. They first restrained Yucheng, his wife Zhou, his third daughter-in-law Chen, and his fifth son Zongren, and shot them all to death. However, Zongmei, who was living in the county town, escaped the attack. Yesterday (the 30th), Zongmei received the news in the city and reported the case to both the garrisoned provincial security regiment and the county government, requesting the arrest of the murderers and justice.

Huzhou Security Team Executes Two Deserters by Firing Squad 113

In the 2nd Regiment, 1st Battalion, 2nd and 3rd Companies of the Huzhou Security Team, two soldiers, Chu Zixing and Chu Junxing, deserted with firearms on the night of the 25th of last month, having agreed to flee together. They were captured by the guards and sent to the regimental headquarters for strict interrogation. They confessed that they had deserted with firearms with the intention of becoming bandits. Commander Shi, based on their confession, believed that the two soldiers were so audacious and disregarded the law, deserving of the severest punishment. He immediately reported to the Security Office and obtained permission to execute them by firing squad. At 10 a.m. yesterday, the two convicts were identified and tied up before being taken to the South Training Ground in the city for execution by firing squad.

Jintan County Government Holds Training for Cooperative Personnel 114

Since County Magistrate Qi Lunjie took office in Jintan, he has actively promoted the organization of cooperatives. More than 70 cooperatives for silkworm rearing, fish farming, irrigation, and consumption have been established, providing considerable relief to the rural economy. In order to rectify the content of each cooperative and achieve perfection, the county government specially convened directors, supervisors, chairmen, and treasurers of each cooperative from January 22nd to 28th, holding short-term training in the county middle school building. They were taught general concepts of cooperation, bookkeeping laws, and knowledge of agricultural bank lending. Moreover, since most of the staff members are township heads and deputies from various districts and towns, as well as people of good repute in rural areas, and silkworm rearing cooperatives account for about three-quarters of the total, experts were also hired to lecture on rural autonomy and sericulture, as a guideline for promoting autonomy and improving sericulture in the future. All expenses for meals and accommodation for the trainees were provided by the county government. The opening ceremony was held at 8 a.m. on the 22nd, with 193 trainees from various cooperatives attending, as well as Wang Xizeng, a representative from the Department of Civil Affairs, Tong Yumin, a representative from the Department of Construction, and more than 40 representatives from various agencies. After the ceremony, Chairman Qi Lunjie, the county magistrate, reported on the significance of the training, and the representatives from the Department of Civil Affairs and the Department of Construction delivered exhortations. Subsequently, representatives from various agencies, Wang Yu, Liu Zhenqun, Tang Chengsi, Zhao Zezhou, and Han Dasou, delivered speeches one after another, with many warnings. Experts and celebrities were invited to give lectures on the 29th.

Local News

Sino-British Communication Officially Opened Yesterday 115

=A Tea Party was Held to Celebrate that Evening=

=Marconi of the West Sent Cables of Congratulations=

According to the Central News Agency, the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, Zhenru Radio Station, has added wireless equipment for direct Sino-British communication. Since the foundation was laid and construction began in June of last year, it was completed at the end of last year. After a successful trial broadcast, the opening ceremony was held at 3 p.m. yesterday. Zhu Jia-hua, Minister of Communications, came to Shanghai from Beijing to preside over the ceremony, and Mrs. Zhu, Ms. Cheng Peifen, personally performed the unveiling ceremony. Yesterday, those who attended, in addition to Wu Tiecheng and others, representatives from the Central Government and the National Government, and the British Consul General, Mr. Brenan, included more than 200 Chinese and foreign guests. After the unveiling ceremony, guests were invited to visit the electrical equipment. From 6 p.m. to 8 p.m., Minister Zhu also held a tea party at No. 80 Seymour Road to celebrate. Details are recorded below:

Venue Arrangement 116

The International Wireless Radio Station is located north of Zhenru Railway Station, covering an area of more than 200 mu (unit of area). The main entrance faces the Zhenpu River, connected by a wooden bridge. The national emblem is crossed at the entrance. Inside the venue, national flags are hung on the antenna towers. The venue is located east of the radio room, with a temporary bamboo shed built. The flag of the Ministry of Communications with its electric symbol is hung in front of the main entrance of the radio room, with a portrait of Sun Yat-sen and the Party and National flags above it. Below is the platform. The walls inside the venue are covered with the flags of England, Germany, America, and France. To the left of the platform is the orchestra.

Strict Security 117

Yesterday afternoon, the Municipal Security Bureau dispatched the 1st Brigade of the Security Team and the Patrol Team to provide security. Extra police officers were also assigned along Zhenru Road to direct traffic. The order was very good. Moreover, the Zhenru Fire Brigade sent two fire trucks to the venue to prevent accidents.

Guest List 118

Yesterday, in addition to the Minister of Communications Zhu Jia-hua and his wife, guests included Wu Tiecheng, representative of the Central Government and the National Government and Mayor of Shanghai; Chu Minyi, representative of the Executive Yuan; Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce; Huang Boqiao, Director of the Two Roads Bureau; Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Shanghai Municipal Government; Xu Peihuang, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau; Wen Hongen, Director of the Public Security Bureau; and Shi Liangcai, as well as Brenan, the British Consul-General in Shanghai, and Massey, the Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce, and diplomatic officials and chamber of commerce representatives from various countries, totaling approximately 200 people.

Opening Ceremony 119

Minister of Communications Zhu Jia-hua, Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Secretary-General of the Executive Yuan Chu Minyi, British Consul-General Brenan, Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce Massey, and Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai, and Mrs. Zhu Cheng Peifen successively ascended the platform. The ceremony was presided over by Minister Zhu, with Lu Hongxun, Chief of the General Affairs Section of the International Telecommunications Bureau, as the master of ceremonies. The Public Security Bureau Military Band played music. After the formalities, Minister Zhu delivered the opening speech, followed by an address by Mayor Wu, representative of the Central Government and the National Government. Subsequently, guests Chu Minyi, representative of the Executive Yuan, British Consul-General Brenan, Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce Massey, and Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Wang Xiaolai delivered speeches one after another, expressing enthusiastic sentiments regarding central diplomatic relations and commerce. The foreign guests present applauded to show their welcome.

Chairman's Report 120

After the ceremony, Chairman Zhu reported, "Since the Sino-British Radio Station began construction in January of last year, all projects were completed by the end of last year. After multiple tests, the results were very good. Today, we are holding the opening ceremony to officially begin communication. From now on, Sino-British wireless telecommunications can be directly connected. Before today, Sino-British telecommunications could only be directly connected through foreign-operated submarine cables. As for the transmission of wireless telecommunications, it was only transferred through Sino-French or Sino-German lines. There was no direct communication equipment. This biased situation makes us very regretful. The development of China's international telecommunications initially relied on submarine cables, and the Sino-British submarine cable telecommunications equipment was the earliest to operate. However, since China built the International Wireless Radio Station in the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931), it automatically began to develop international wireless telecommunications in order to seek closer contact with the world. Subsequently, direct wireless communication was established with the United States, France, Germany, Russia, and Switzerland. Even Manila and Batavia can directly communicate using wireless telecommunications. However, Sino-British telecommunications, which utilized submarine cables the earliest, lagged behind in wireless telecommunications. Isn't this something to be regretted? Therefore, we quickly devised a way to add this Sino-British Radio Station, so that China and Britain have the same connection as other countries in wireless communication, and we hope that the entire connection of China's wireless communication with the world can be completed. The completion of this Sino-British Radio Station has even deeper significance, worthy of careful consideration. The close relationship between China and Britain has always been evident. We can see it from the reporting. According to our statistics, the telegrams between China and London each year account for more than half of our total European reporting revenue. From this statistic alone, we can see how close the relationship is. We attach importance to this close relationship. We especially attach importance to China and Britain using this close relationship to increase cooperation and mutual assistance, because both China and Britain need mutual assistance in education, culture, and economy. The purpose of building the Sino-British Radio Station is to hope that this friendship and cooperation will have more convenience in material equipment, and we hope to use this convenience of material equipment to make the friendship and cooperation between China and Britain closer. Looking at this year, although China is experiencing internal and external troubles and financial difficulties, the construction of this Sino-British Radio Station has not been interrupted due to environmental difficulties. This shows how much we hope for the mission of the Sino-British Radio Station. Now that the Central Radio Station has been completed, we

Iron Tower of the Zhenru Wireless Radio Station 121

(Photographed by Yingming Photography Studio)

believe that its effect will surely reach the realm jointly expected by the two countries. Today, we are holding the opening ceremony, and we are very honored to have all the guests present to participate. However, this Sino-British Radio Station is in its initial stage, and there must be many shortcomings. We hope that everyone will not hesitate to correct us."

Wu's Address 122

After Minister Zhu's report, Wu Tiecheng, representative of the Central Party Department and the National Government and Mayor of Shanghai, delivered an address, saying, "Today, the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications is holding the opening ceremony of the Sino-British direct circuit. I am honored to be ordered by the Central Government to participate in this grand ceremony, and I would like to express my hopes. We use a historical perspective to observe that the development of transportation is truly a great driving force for the progress of modern countries. Just looking at the two points of post and telecommunications, from 1881 to 1913, the number of post offices in Britain increased from 15,400 to 24,600, in France from 6,700 to 15,700, and in Germany from 12,500 to 51,600. At the same time, the average number of mail items per year for each person in the country increased from 40 to 96 in Britain, from 16 to 40 in France, and from 17 to 80 in Germany. The development and increase in these numbers of mail items can measure the degree of political progress in modern European countries. Modern international relations are becoming increasingly complex, and the opportunities and needs for mutual assistance and cooperation among nations are also increasing. Therefore, post and telecommunications are naturally indispensable tools for improving international relations and promoting national sentiments. The British historian H.G. Wells once said that the reason why Central European nations cannot understand each other is due to the separation of their circumstances. We must naturally strive to make up for and eliminate this international defect. The Chinese proverb says that human determination can overcome nature. Modern material civilization and the development of transportation have already broken through the natural and material obstacles in the universe that were previously unbreakable by humans. Why can't we go a step further to strive to eliminate the emotional and spiritual barriers between nations? Therefore, today's opening of the Sino-British direct circuit of the International Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications represents the beginning of the Chinese nation's efforts to eliminate national barriers and make up for international defects. After the Sino-British direct circuit, it will not only increase the convenience of mutual communication between the two major nations of China and Britain, but also promote the harmony between the two major nations of China and Britain.

Wang's Speech 123

Wang Xiaolai, Chairman of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, said in his speech, "Today is the opening ceremony for the Sino-British direct line of the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications. In other words, it can be said that China has won a speaking mouth in Europe. We often hear people say that when it comes to military operations, the most important thing is the seaport, because with a seaport, transportation is convenient, so the first step in a war is to blockade the seaport. Once the seaport is blockaded, you cannot enter or exit, as if you are holding someone's throat, and this person will inevitably suffocate. But we must know that the current world is not just a world of war with weapons, but also a world that pays attention to the work of publicity. But when it comes to publicity, you must have a mouth. If you are a mute and rely on others to speak, sometimes the things you want to say, people will not say for you, or the things you don't want to say, people will spread them everywhere. Over time, what is false becomes true, and you have a belly full of grievances, and where can you vent them? I think, not to mention malicious publicity, deliberately reversing right and wrong, even unintentional mistakes can greatly affect you. Then, what is the mouth of propaganda now? It is the international telecommunications business. For forty years, my country's international telecommunications business has always been operated by foreign submarine cable companies. If we want to speak to foreigners, we must first go through the throats of foreigners. This is really inconvenient. I think, to put it lightly, it is called the outflow of rights and interests, and to put it more seriously, it is simply inverting the dagger. The outflow of rights and interests is the loss of the benefits of telecommunications, and inverting the dagger is the loss of the power of telecommunications. So often there are many things that are clearly so and so, but when they are transmitted to foreign countries, they become this and that. The most ridiculous thing is that even Chinese ambassadors and consuls abroad have to ask foreign telecommunications agencies to know the news of their own country. Do you all think it is ridiculous? Therefore, the National Government, when it was in Guangdong, had already noticed this point. From the 18th to the 23rd year of the Republic of China (1929 to 1934), in these six years, through the continuous efforts of the Ministry of Communications, it expanded the direct communication lines from Shanghai to nine places including Manila, Hong Kong, Batavia, San Francisco, Berlin, Paris, Saigon, Geneva, and Moscow. Now it has added the direct line between Shanghai and London. We know that Shanghai is the telecommunications hub of China, and London is the telecommunications hub of Europe. Therefore, the direct line between Shanghai and London, I said at the beginning, is that China has won a speaking mouth in Europe. This is of course something to be congratulated on.

Minister Zhu's Report (Photographed by Xu Tianzhang) 124

White's Speech 125

Next, British Consul General Mr. Brenan and Mr. Massey successively delivered speeches. Mr. Brenan said in his speech, "Everyone who is present to participate in the grand ceremony of the first direct communication between China and Britain today must feel happy. China and Britain have a long and good history in diplomatic, cultural and commercial relations. Now that the direct communication report is completed, there will be a cheap, high-quality and rapid transportation system between the two countries from now on, and its benefits to the increase of friendship between the two countries are even more profound. In the past, communication between Europe and Asia was only by ships, and it took six months to get a reply. Today, the situation has changed greatly. The invention of steamships, the opening of the Suez Canal, the establishment of submarine telegraph cables, and the success of wireless radio have made the close relationship between China and Britain today incomparable to the past, and the trade between the two countries occupies an important position in international politics. Some people may say that foreign representatives like me should not welcome the tools that facilitate transportation, because in the past, when communication was inconvenient, the power of each representative was greater. Today, even minor matters need to be referred to the government, and those who are local representatives are, at best, puppets who only listen to orders. Whether this statement is true or not, I will not discuss it for the time being, but I am very willing to communicate with the people on the other end of the radio waves. Therefore, I express my sincere congratulations on the completion of this station, and I deeply believe that it will make immeasurable contributions to the future of Sino-British commerce, and I am happy to congratulate Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Communications even more."

Massey's Speech 126

Minister, Ladies and Gentlemen, the British Boxer Indemnity Committee, the British Chamber of Commerce, and the Joint Committee of the Associated British Chambers of Commerce, although they are two different organizations, they all pay close attention to businesses that are mutually beneficial to China and Britain. As the Vice Chairman of the British Boxer Indemnity Committee, I deeply feel that the Committee's loan to the Ministry of Communications to purchase the various equipment needed for this radio station has truly benefited China and Britain. At the same time, from the perspective of the Chairman of the British Chamber of Commerce, I especially believe that the official opening of direct communication between China and Britain can promote commerce and greatly help merchants who need rapid and reliable services. On behalf of the two organizations, I congratulate Minister Yan, Director Wen, and all the colleagues of the Ministry of Communications for their efforts to make the direct communication between China and Britain a success. As the saying goes, time is money. The accuracy of this saying is almost unsurpassed today. The more advanced commerce is, the more it needs faster and more reliable transportation services. The Ministry of Communications, in view of this, established this radio station to connect direct transportation between China and Britain. The machines used are all the latest Marconi type, and all the advances in scientific research are available, which is truly suitable for the needs of all merchants. The direct communication between China and Britain is no longer relayed by Paris or Berlin. The transmission is faster and can avoid the errors of wired telegraphs. The convenience is obvious. It is said that the characteristic of this radio station is the principle of grabbing light bands. This principle was discovered by Marconi. Before, when Mr. Marconi came to China and visited the Zhenru Radio Station, he greatly praised the beauty of the Chinese engineering construction project. One of the most interesting features of this station is wireless telephone. This telephone is currently limited to international speeches or music broadcasts. I hope that this convenience can be expanded to commercial telephone, so that we can talk directly to London. The advantage of telephone is that a few minutes of talk can often eliminate many difficulties that telegrams cannot. If the call can be made early, it will benefit merchants greatly. The authorities of the Ministry of Communications know that the success of the radio station depends on the engineers being familiar with everything. Therefore, in addition to adopting the latest machines, they also specially sent four engineers to England to investigate and study everything. They are familiar with all the usage methods of the Marconi light band radio station. After studying at the Marconi Engineering School, they went to various places and radio stations to investigate. After the engineers returned to China, they were assigned to important positions in this radio station. In the future, the control and management will be easy to handle. Minister Zhu's enthusiasm for the future of transportation is truly a great reliance on national construction.

Telegrams of Congratulation from the British Side 130

British Foreign Secretary, Postmaster General, and radio inventor Marconi, among others, have sent telegrams of congratulations. Details of congratulatory telegrams exchanged between Britain and our country are as follows:

(1) British Foreign Secretary Simon to the Minister of Foreign Affairs: "On this occasion of the first direct radio communication between London and Shanghai, I extend to Your Excellency this telegram of congratulations. I am particularly pleased, as the relationship between China and Britain has been constantly in my thoughts lately. I have discussed everything with Sir Lampson and Sir O’Malley, who is about to go to your country. I am confident that the special and excellent relationship between the two countries created by Sir Lampson during his previous residency in China will be fully maintained during Sir O’Malley’s term. This new method of communication is itself a clear demonstration of Sino-British cooperation, and will further enhance all the points we cherish, such as friendship between the two countries, mutual understanding, and commercial and cultural ties."

(2) President Wang's reply to the British Foreign Secretary: "To His Excellency Sir John Simon, British Foreign Secretary, upon receiving your telegram, I learned that Your Excellency, on behalf of the British government, extended congratulations on the first direct Sino-British radio communication. I am deeply grateful. Your Excellency's close attention to the relationship between China and Britain is particularly appreciated. I also concur with your statement that the special and excellent relationship between the two countries created by Sir Lampson during his previous residency in China will be fully maintained during Sir O’Malley’s upcoming term in China. I firmly believe that this new method of communication will enhance mutual understanding between the two countries and further solidify their friendship, which is crucial for peace and prosperity in the Far East."

(3) British Postmaster General to Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Transportation: "To His Excellency Minister Zhu of Transportation, Nanjing, on this grand occasion of the opening of direct radio telegraph service between London and Shanghai, I am deeply pleased that the improvement of Sino-British communication has taken a further step. I believe this newly added convenience will greatly benefit both countries and further increase the existing volume of telegram traffic between the two countries. Therefore, I respectfully wish success to this new circuit and feel extremely delighted. British Postmaster General."

(4) Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Transportation replies to the British Postmaster General, Mr. Wood: "To His Excellency Mr. Wood, British Postmaster General, London, upon the opening of direct radio telegraph service between London and Shanghai, I am honored to receive your gracious telegram and carefully considered it. I share your view that this benefits both countries. I hope that this newly established instrument will enhance the inherent friendship and commercial relations between China and Britain. Zhu Jiahua, Minister of Transportation, China."

(5) Marquis Marconi to our Minister of Transportation (sent from London): "To His Excellency the Minister of Transportation, Nanjing, having just returned to Europe from my tour of China, I am especially pleased to send this congratulatory telegram via radio upon the inauguration of the Shanghai direct radio station and the opening of direct radio communication between the United States and China. During my visit to the Zhenru Radio Station and my pleasant journey in your country, I observed everywhere that your government attaches great importance to the development of domestic and international transportation, which is noteworthy. I am particularly gratified by the abundant technical capabilities of your engineers and telegraph operators who manage this new enterprise. Under these circumstances, I firmly believe that this newly added direct connection between the two countries will be fully successful in all aspects and will consolidate and enhance the mutual interests of the two countries. To Your Excellency personally, on this occasion of the successful completion of a major achievement in China's transportation development, I extend my warmest congratulations and take this opportunity to express my sincere gratitude for the cordial welcome that Your Excellency and the people of your country extended to my wife and me. We will forever cherish the pleasant memories of China and its spirit of progress. Your country's adoption of this modern instrument to connect with the most distant countries in the world is a clear manifestation of your spirit of progress. Marquis Marconi."

(6) Minister Zhu of the Ministry of Transportation replies to Marquis Marconi: "To His Excellency Marquis Marconi, London, I am honored to receive your congratulatory telegram regarding the direct radio communication between Shanghai and London. I am deeply grateful for your insightful observations on your trip to China. I sincerely and on behalf of my colleagues in the Ministry, take this opportunity to wish you and your wife health and happiness. At the same time, we deeply admire your valuable assistance and your company's satisfactory service in the construction of the Sino-British radio cooperation.
