Dongwu Night School Submits a Request to the Ministry of Education to Continue Operations 226

After the Ministry of Education issued an order for five schools in this city, including Dongwu, Chizhi, Hujiang, and Fazheng, to discontinue their night schools, each school has now decided not to admit new students. However, the methods of closure vary. The Fazheng School authorities plan to convene a meeting of representatives from each school to discuss response strategies. The Shen Shi News reporter met with Ren Qun, the chairman of the student union of the Dongwu Law School, yesterday to inquire about everything in detail. According to him, the regulations of Dongwu and other night schools stipulate that those applying to the night school must have a bachelor's degree from a national or officially registered private university. Therefore, all night school students have completed military training early in accordance with the Ministry of Education's regulations. Even those who already have doctoral or master's degrees in other fields must study for a full three years before graduating. Thus, anyone who obtains a law degree from the night school must have undergone at least seven years of university education. Moreover, the curriculum is well-designed, no different from the night schools established by New York University and Northwestern University in the United States. In addition to domestic law, the curriculum also includes the laws of countries such as England, America, Japan, Germany, and Italy for reference and comparison. The examination regulations adopt the system of Cambridge University in England, which is a first in the country. A strict approach is always adopted. Any student who is absent for more than 30 hours per semester will not receive full credit for all courses. Therefore, all students are diligent and hardworking. Recently, the school launched a large-scale fundraising campaign to build the most comprehensive law library in East Asia with 300,000 yuan, so that domestic scholars can observe and learn. It is heard that most of the total funds have been raised, and construction may begin next semester. Furthermore, graduates of the night school over the years have been highly regarded by society, and various universities in Europe and America can formally recognize them. If they go abroad for further study for one year, they will be granted a doctoral degree. The Shen Shi News reporter inquired with the school authorities about future plans. According to them, the school does not typically enroll students during the winter vacation. The school is not participating in the meeting of representatives from various schools convened by Fazheng. They are currently submitting a report to the Ministry of Education, stating that the establishment of the night school does not violate the Ministry's regulations and requesting that it be allowed to continue operating.

The Truth About Donghua Club's Withdrawal from the War 228

Li Ning is Penalized, and the Sports Association Does Not Protest on Their Behalf

Failing to Announce It the Night Before is Like Intentionally Sabotaging

Going Against the Press is a Poor Strategy for the Team Donghua Club's temporary absence from the baseball field for the match against the French Merchants has sparked criticism from many quarters. Indeed, given Donghua's status and reputation, it seems inappropriate to engage in such a frivolous act. Donghua certainly has its own grievances and reasons, but whether it can gain forgiveness from the outside world remains to be seen.

Great Disappointment Due to the French Merchants' recent two defeats, yesterday's match against Donghua was considered a great opportunity for Donghua to contend for supremacy. Fans were enthusiastic, but finding the doors closed upon arrival was truly disappointing. Donghua's absence is said to be due to Li Ning's suspension and Wan Xianghua's absence due to his expedition to the north, resulting in an insufficient number of players. However, why not plan ahead and avoid a last-minute change of plans? The strangest thing is that Donghua informed the Western newspapers of its inability to attend in advance. When Chinese newspaper reporters inquired about the lineup the night before, they were neither informed of who would replace Li and Wan nor given any indication that they would be unable to attend. This is truly perplexing.

No One in Charge According to Zhou Jiaqi, an official of the Sports Advancement Association, after seeing a Western newspaper report at 8:30 a.m. that Donghua might not be able to attend, he rushed to Donghua to inquire about the truth. He first asked the team captain, Tu Kaiyuan, who said that he only knew about selecting the field and other matters and knew nothing else. He then asked the administrator, Lu Zhong'en, who replied that he did not know. Thus, there was no indication whether the team would attend.

When asked again at 10:30 a.m., there was still no result. It was not until around 11:00 a.m. that Lu Zhong'en replied that there was no one available and that a decision could not be made until 3:00 p.m. Later, at 2:35 p.m., the official reply from Lu Zhong'en of the club was finally received, stating that they had decided not to attend.

Strange

Furthermore, according to a statement from a Donghua spokesperson, Li Ning was penalized for two weeks for representing the Chinese team in the International Football Tournament. Donghua was dissatisfied and requested an appeal, but since Li represented the Chinese team, the appeal had to be made by the Chinese team. Donghua then requested the Sports Advancement Association to protest on their behalf, but the Sports Advancement Association did not immediately do so, leading to dissatisfaction. The team also asked the Western Union that night whether the date could be changed, but the Western Union secretary stated that the schedule had already been arranged and could not be changed at the last minute, so the match had to be played. Donghua then decided not to attend, but when Chinese newspaper reporters inquired the night before, they did not directly inform them of their inability to attend and instead informed the Western newspapers. Furthermore, until 2:00 p.m. yesterday, when the Sports Advancement Association inquired whether they would attend, they consistently refused to reveal the truth until 2:35 p.m., which was tantamount to intentionally making things difficult for the Chinese newspapers and the Sports Advancement Association. It is believed that Donghua should not have done this.

Jinan Loses to the Western Merchants in an Upset 229

Old Generals Return Home, Forcing a Makeshift Team

Mei Hongbao Acts as Goalkeeper

Leading by One Goal Before Conceding Three Since the key players of the Jinan Football Team, such as Xu Heng, Gu Shangxiong, and Chen Zhenxiang, returned home for the winter vacation, their strength has been greatly reduced. Recently, Xu Yahui and others have also returned home. Therefore, in yesterday's match against the Western Merchants at Yiyuan, they used players from the B team and formed a makeshift team. Mei Hongbao played as a guest goalkeeper, and Luo Haiguang retreated to play defense. The situation was lackluster, and the interest was reduced. Although Jinan scored first within five minutes of the start, they ultimately lost 1-3.

Opening the Scoring

The young players of Jinan were indeed spirited and showed no weakness. Within five minutes, they scored the first goal. The goal was scored when center Chen Bin dribbled the ball forward, dribbled past the Western Merchant's Hou Faping, and goalkeeper Godekin rushed out to intercept the ball, missing completely. The ball landed on the goal line, and Qiu Zhen'an rushed up and put it in, opening the scoring. After the Western Merchants kicked off, their left wing went deep and passed the ball to the front of the goal. The Jinan defender missed, and Mei Hongbao also failed to catch it. In the blink of an eye, the ball was at the right corner of the goal, less than a yard from the goal. The Western Merchant's right wing, Atai, rushed to the spot and was about to score, but he was too hasty and shot the ball wide, causing the spectators to burst into laughter.

Losing Again and Again, the Situation Becomes Dull Around half an hour later, the Western Merchant's Stoke sent the ball from the center to the right. Right wing Atai broke through two defenders and crossed the ball from the baseline. The Jinan defender could not get back in time, and Haitley had already chased to the goal, taking advantage of the situation to poke the ball in. Mei Hongbao was caught off guard, and the goal was conceded. The first half ended in a 1-1 draw. After the start of the second half, the Western Merchants' momentum suddenly increased, and their attack was extremely fierce. Jinan was busy defending and had no time to attack. Although Mei Hongbao was able to save many dangerous shots, he was ultimately scored on by Jin Bo, and Jinan succumbed by a score of 1-2.

The Referee is Insulted Jinan has become an oppressed and weak nation. The forwards are isolated and helpless, merely wishing they had more strength than they did. The Western Merchants are on the rise and are aggressive. Once, Mei Hongbao hugged the ball with both hands and hesitated slightly. The Western Merchant's Haitley rushed up and collided with him, causing him to fall into the goal with the ball. Referee Lennox ruled the goal invalid and penalized the Western Merchants instead, causing resistance and insults from a Western spectator. Later, Jinan was penalized with a penalty kick, and the Western person again scolded the referee for nitpicking. Lennox was furious and ran to the stands to scold the Western person. The Chinese spectators applauded greatly. According to his subsequent explanation, the goal where Mei Hongbao fell into the goal was not counted because Jin Bo used his foot to poke rather than撞 (collision), so the Western Merchants were penalized.

Penalty Kick Stoke took the penalty kick with great force, but it was right at the center of the goal, allowing Mei Hongbao to kick it back out. It was very fortunate that this ball did not go in. Later, Jinan burned their boats and tried to counterattack. Luo Haiguang was changed from inside guard to center back, and then to center forward, intending to make a desperate gamble. However, the attack failed, and the defense was breached again. Haitley received a pass from Atai and attacked, which was very beautiful. As a result, Jinan lost 1-3.

Free Talk

Northerners and Southerners 236

— Le Ting Shi

This was what I thought of after reading the discussions on the "Beijing School" and the "Shanghai School"! The Northerners' contempt for Southerners has become a tradition. This is not merely due to differences in customs. I think the main reason is that historically, invaders mostly came from the north, first conquering the northern part of China, and then carrying the Northerners southward. Thus, in the eyes of Northerners, Southerners are also the conquered. When the Two Lu's entered Jin, the Northerners clearly showed disdain amidst their jubilation. Providing evidence would be too cumbersome, so let's not discuss it for now. It's easier to see that in Yang Jie Zhi's "Records of the Buddhist Temples of Luoyang," Southerners are often disparaged and not regarded as equals. As for the Yuan Dynasty, the people were clearly divided into four classes: first, the Mongols; second, the Semu people; third, the Han people, i.e., the Northerners; and fourth, the Southerners, because they were the last to surrender. Surrendering last, from their perspective, meant exhausting all resources and being forced to cease fighting due to the strength of the South. From the invaders' perspective, however, it meant being ignorant of the times and resisting the king's army for too long. Of course, descendants still surrendered, but their qualification for slavery was the lowest. Because it was low, their rank was the lowest, and everyone could despise them. By the Qing Dynasty, this account was rehashed, and its aftereffects still linger today. If history from now on no longer repeats itself, it would truly be a blessing not only for Southerners.

Of course, Southerners have their shortcomings. When the powerful and wealthy moved south, they brought with them a corrupt and decadent atmosphere, while the North remained relatively clean. Their temperaments are also different. They have shortcomings, but also strengths, just like Northerners possess both. In my opinion, the Northerners' strength is their groundedness, while the Southerners' strength is their agility. However, the downside of groundedness is dullness, and the downside of agility is cunning. Therefore, a certain gentleman once pointed out their shortcomings, saying: Northerners are "full all day and have nothing to occupy their minds"; Southerners are "together all day and never speak of righteousness." As far as the leisure class is concerned, I think this is largely true. Shortcomings can be corrected, and strengths can be learned from each other. There is a saying in physiognomy that a Northerner with Southern features, or a Southerner with Northern features, will be noble. I don't think this is nonsense. A Northerner with Southern features is both grounded and agile, while a Southerner with Northern features is, needless to say, agile and grounded. The so-called "noble" in the past simply meant success in those times. In the present, it means achieving beneficial undertakings. This is a small way for the Chinese to renew themselves. However, Southerners write more articles, and the North has been influenced. Aren't there more glib, evasive, and self-pitying writings in Beijing newspapers than six or seven years ago? If this were to marry with the Northerners' inherent "glibness," the offspring would certainly be an ominous new inferior breed!

Goldfish 237

— Yu Yang Ling

Refined people and the wealthy always like to keep some creatures at home for appreciation. Once they are kept by them, these creatures are generally changed. For example, plum blossoms must be "beautiful in their crookedness, uninteresting when straight; beautiful in their obliqueness, uninspiring when upright; beautiful in their sparseness, lacking charm when dense." Thus, they "chop the straight, thin the dense, and uproot the upright." This was criticized by Gong Ding'an, who believed that what they cultivated were all "sick plum blossoms." As for animals, there is a kind of goldfish, said to be a variation of the carp, also for appreciation.

I have never liked these ornamental creatures, especially looking down on those goldfish with bulging heads and protruding eyes. Every time I see it wriggling in a glass tank, I never believe that it is a living thing. Its wriggling lacks the vitality of splashing around, and does not resemble the movement of a living thing. However, it is this lifeless goldfish that has recently surprised me. A lady living in the same residence keeps such a goldfish, but only one, in a small washbasin. When she was about to return to her hometown, she gave us the goldfish and the washbasin, saying that if we were happy to, we only needed to change the water for it once a day. Although we received it, we found it very funny, thinking that such a thing would die in less than a day, so we casually put it on the windowsill and didn't bother with it at all.

The weather got colder day by day, so cold that all the water in the room froze. One day, I happened to walk to the windowsill and saw that the water in the washbasin was also a block of ice, so I thought to myself that the goldfish must be dead. Taking a closer look, it was lying on top of the ice block on the edge of the washbasin, still wriggling, not dead. This surprised me greatly, and at the same time, I felt a little sympathy, melted the ice for it, and changed the water. But the next day, the water still froze, the third day, the fourth day... it was like this for several days in a row, and the goldfish was finally unharmed, and is still wriggling without vitality to this day.

I am most prone to making a fuss over nothing. I have thought about this for a long time, and at the same time, I thought of Nietzsche's words in "The Will to Power": "Nature is cruel to the darlings of fate... but nature is tolerant, protective, and cherishing of lowly things... middle and even lower species. Therefore, the latter often have great reproductive power and survivability, while the former are destroyed very quickly and their numbers decrease." I think it is very true. At the same time, I also thought that the Chinese people, in extreme poverty and harsh environments, can still reproduce and survive, which can also be said to be divinely favored, almost like goldfish. They are both fit for survival in the struggle for existence. Will such a Chinese nation become a nation dedicated to appreciation like goldfish in the future? But that would still be considered good. I am only afraid that it will become a poisonous fungus. Fungi are extremely low-level organisms, and their reproductive power and survivability are also the greatest.

Home 238

— Ren Bai Ge

Even chickens have a hen-house. Even dogs have a kennel. Even pigs have a sty. Yet, I have no home.

Home, my home lying in the embrace of green mountains, my home hiding behind green bamboos, I hear it is still there. The gentle valley breeze, the lazy sun, the crowing of chickens, the puffs of green smoke, I imagine are still there, and are blowing, shining, calling, and rising. Yet, I am not there. To turn it around, home has no me.

To say that I have no home, the home is still there; to say that I have a home, the home has no me. Sometimes, even I am a little confused, finding it difficult to answer all those who love me and therefore ask about my home. Yet, my grandmother's smile is gone, my uncle's candies are gone, my father's gentle concern is gone, my siblings' playfulness is gone, and I can only say this: I have no home.

Perhaps I was born a few decades too early? Perhaps I was born a few centuries too late? Watching my father's farmland decrease day by day, watching my father's face age day by day, watching my father's sighs increase day by day, watching my father's temperament become more irritable day by day, I could not bear to accompany him in that change for long. I could only leave him reluctantly for a while, and go far away. From then on, home had no me.

Years of wandering have made it easy for me to miss home all the time. I miss my grandmother, who is nearly a hundred years old. I miss my uncle, who is all alone. I miss my father, who has been widowed for half his life. I miss my younger siblings, who lost their infancy. Yet, I cannot help but go far away, even if I have a home, I cannot return.

There are many people in the world who have no home to return to. Yet, I envy their happiness of being homeless. At most, they have only tasted the sadness of loneliness. I have to taste the sadness beyond this loneliness! At the very least, I have to shed another tear for my longing for home. Because on the burden of emotion, I am still burdened with a home that I miss.

Now, here, I can imagine my father is living the life of a serf in the Middle Ages (although we were born in the country that claims to be the earliest civilized in the so-called civilized twentieth century). The grain tax of more than ten times a year requires his blood and sweat to pay. The conscription of more than ten times a month requires his blood and sweat to provide. All kinds of exorbitant taxes have already bent his old bones. Yet, he still has to use his few bent old bones to support the home I miss. Little does he know that the home I miss has long been destroyed, and I have long had no home.

Fleeting clouds of worldly affairs, ripples of life, can I be allowed to drift in the air for a long time, or draw a few more circles on the water? I cannot be without a home forever. But I hope everyone has one, and it is gentle and sweet.

Liang Ren Gong in Hunan 239

— Yu Shi Xia

"Four feet in the air, let's see what you can do!"

"Listening with one ear, in the end it's nothing!"

This is a humorous couplet used by the conservative faction in Hunan to mock Chen Baozhen and Xiong Xiling after the failure of the Hundred Days' Reform, taking apart the characters of Xiong and Chen, which is quite interesting. Originally, the Hundred Days' Reform movement in Hunan was jointly organized by officials and gentry, with Chen Zhongcheng representing the official side and Xiong Shuchang representing the gentry side. In this movement, Kang and Liang were the main figures. Kang Youwei was in Beijing, gaining the trust of Emperor Guangxu, so the situation in Beijing was very intense. Liang Qichao was in Hunan, gaining the trust of Chen Zhongcheng, so the situation in Hunan was also very intense. Why did Mr. Liang come to Hunan? According to Xiong Xiling's letter to Chen Zhongcheng, the invitation of Liang Zhuoru as an instructor originated from Huang Gongdu (Huang Zunxian, then the Hunan Salt Commissioner), and Zou Yuanfan and Ling and Boyan (Chen Sanli, Chen Zhongcheng's son) all agreed. Mr. Liang came to Hunan, presided over the Academy of Current Affairs, and became the chief instructor. Han Wenju and Ye Juemai, who came with him, became instructors, and the Kang faction's power was at its peak for a time. Moreover, all the teachers and students in the academy praised each other, saying either "the people who teach today are those who will assist the dynasty in its revival," or "those who will take on difficult tasks in the future are all sixteen-year-old children from the academy." This was really enough to make the conservative faction's eyes burn with fire. What's more, the diary of the Academy of Current Affairs, the comments on the course exercises, the lectures of the South Society, and the articles published in the Xiang Bao and the Xiang Xue Bao were all Kang faction's arguments that the conservative faction regarded as heresy!

Naturally, those arguments that were regarded as heresy, when viewed today more than thirty years later, are inevitably commonplace, shallow, and ridiculous. But in those days, they inevitably felt like earth-shattering events! For example, Mr. Liang commented on a diary, saying:

"Of the twenty-four dynasties, no one is worthy of Confucius' title of king. Occasionally, a few hegemons were born among them, and the rest were all traitors to the people."

Condemning all emperors as traitors to the people, and only acknowledging a few hegemons among them, this could not but shock the Confucian scholars. Another comment on a question-and-answer: "A minister is one who handles civil affairs with the ruler. It's like opening a shop. The ruler is the manager of the shop, and the minister is the shopkeeper, etc." Although Mr. Liang did not say that the people are the major shareholders of this shop, he already did not recognize the "righteousness of the ruler and minister" that Confucian scholars had always talked about. Another comment on a course exercise: "The Spring and Autumn Great Harmony learning all speaks of the rights of the people. Why not extract the rights of the people mentioned in the Six Classics and compile them into a book? It would also be a grand sight."

Mr. Liang advocated for the rights of the people and made many arguments. For example, he commented on a diary, saying:

"If public law wants to take a country, it must first have the great support of the people, and then that country can be taken by me. Therefore, those who can promote the rights of the people can never perish." He also said: "Although the parliament originated in the West, in fact, the meaning of it is mostly found in the biographies of the Five Classics and the philosophers. It is a pity that the rule of the monarch is too long, and no one dares to speak of it!" Mr. Liang wanted to advocate for parliamentary politics. He advocated for the rights of the people and parliament, but he could not help but resort to the Five Classics and Six Classics. Now we may laugh at his pedantry, but when we think of him in the environment at the time, we cannot help but forgive his painstaking efforts. He commented on a course exercise: "Today, if we want to seek reform, we must start with the emperor lowering his dignity. If we do not first change the etiquette of bowing and kneeling, and superiors and inferiors still practice empty formalities, we will be laughed at by foreign countries for everything we do." Mr. Liang boldly advocated for the emperor to lower his dignity and abolish the etiquette of bowing and kneeling. He also commented on a diary, saying: "China's bandits are very rampant. Superiors have no etiquette, and inferiors have no learning. The people rebel, and there will be no day of mourning. Today's reform must first change the laws and regulations. Although clothing is a trivial matter, it is closest to the human body. Therefore, there has never been a reform that did not first change clothing. If this can be changed, nothing cannot be changed." Mr. Liang advocated for changing the laws and regulations and changing clothing, which were all bold words, and all of them were going to be attacked by the conservative faction in Hunan. Strangely, the temperament of the people of Hunan is to go to extremes. From the Hundred Days' Reform to the present, in every political change, the people of Hunan are always at the forefront of the opposing extremes. In the Hundred Days' Reform, Tan Sitong, Xiong Xiling and others stood at the forefront of the reformist faction; Ye Dehui, Wang Yiwu and others stood at the forefront of the conservative faction. During the Wuchang Uprising of the Xinhai Revolution, Hunan was the first to respond, but Huang Zhonghao, the first general to die for the Manchu Qing, was also from Hunan. When Yuan Shikai proclaimed himself emperor, Yang Du, the leader of the Preparatory Council, was from Hunan, and Cai E, who was at the forefront of the campaign against Yuan, was also from Hunan.

Understanding the temperament of the people of Hunan, one understands the Hundred Days' Reform. Liang Rengong in Hunan had to be warmly welcomed by the reformist faction on the one hand, and frantically attacked by the conservative faction on the other.

Nanny (2) 240

— Xu Zhuan Peng

As she walked through the back door, the female cook saw her and asked, "Are you the nanny?" She carefully replied, "Yes! What is your sister-in-law to this family?" "I am a maidservant. We will be eating in the same room in the future..." The female cook, who was around forty years old, saw the young nanny and treated her as if she were her own daughter. "Come and sit in the kitchen for a while, the madam hasn't gotten up yet!" The female cook led her to the kitchen. She was plunged into an unfamiliar environment, like a fish thrown onto mud. Her movements and eyes were dull, and she sat there like a blockhead. Soon, she heard a sobbing sound upstairs, as if someone were choking the throat. The female cook turned to the nanny and said, "This is the crying child... a rare child who cries so much... He's fine during the day, but he chooses to cry at night. He cried non-stop last night..." "Maybe it's because he doesn't have milk to eat." "The madam had a lot of milk when he was first born for two months." The female cook deliberately softened her tone and said with a nasal sound, "She got pregnant again in the third month..." "Why didn't you hire a nanny sooner?" she asked indifferently. "The previous nanny just left three days ago. She quit after only a week." "Why did she quit?" "..." The female cook answered with a long, mysterious smile. The new nanny stood in front of the madam. The madam's brain left a deep impression of her. A dark face, unclean clothes... The dirt behind her ears and on her neck did not escape the madam's sharp eyes

Silk and Tea: Last Year's Chinese Silk Export Figures Increased 260

(An increase of over 61,000 bales)

In recent years, Chinese silk exports have plummeted due to the encroachment of Japanese silk and rayon. It was not until last year that it began to improve slightly. In the 22nd year, a total of 209,101 dan of yellow, white, and gray silks were exported, while in the previous year (the 21st year), it was only 147,624 dan, an increase of 61,477 dan.

(American Silk Weaving Factory Resumes Work)

American silk weaving factories have been reducing labor and stopping machines due to the global economic recession last year, the sluggish sales of silk fabrics, and the thick inventory. With the start of spring sales this year, the market has gradually turned around, so the silk weaving factories are now preparing to gradually resume work, and the consumption of raw silk is gradually increasing. (New York Silk Telegrams Continue to Transfer to Shanghai) The spring sales orders for overseas silk weaving factories have arrived, and the sales and consumption of raw silk are gradually increasing, and the appetite is gradually rising. The yellow, white, and factory silks initially sent to New York and other places by various European banks in Shanghai have continued to transfer to Shanghai since yesterday morning via telegrams. Unfortunately, the incoming price of B-grade white factory silk is only 567 yuan, and it is still difficult for the factories to sell, and negotiations are still difficult to reach an agreement. Yesterday, only Xinfu and other firms entered 60 bales of Shanghai white factory silk, and the price trend was firm and stable.

Thought and Power 281

— Gongpu

Thought and power have a mutual relationship, and the rise and fall of power must be directly proportional to the expression of thought. This situation can be seen in the actions of an individual, and it can be seen even more clearly in the actions of a group of people. In ancient and modern history, the clearest examples of a group demonstrating great power through the convergence of thought fall into two major categories: (1) religion; and (2) the nation. Although there are often causal relationships between these, there is no doubt that the formation of much power in the past originated from the two major ideas of religion and the nation. As for the many sociologists today who analyze the factors that form these two ideas, there are many similarities, and the historical manifestations of religious and national power were often exploited by a minority and followed blindly by the masses, etc., all of which are beyond the scope of this article.

Where there is thought, there is power, so thought is the source of power. Because of geographical, printing, and other obstacles, the spread of ideas in ancient times was not as convenient as it is today, so the establishment of a new idea and the destruction of an old power were not easy tasks. But today's situation is different. When we compare the recent situation of Soviet Russia with the generally backward state of culture of the Russian people in the past, it is truly astonishing (see Stalin's report at the Soviet Russian Communist Party Congress). Secondly, the success of the Italian Blackshirts and the recent victory of Hitler's dictatorship in Germany are both colorful expressions in modern history! It is an example of how the masses of people in several countries with different languages and histories can quickly form a great force from the spread of an idea.

Any idea that meets the needs of the majority of the masses can always gain the belief and power of the masses, and the prerequisite for gaining this belief and power lies in the ability to find the right people to lead this ideological movement and to use it effectively. Although the political ideas of the political transformations in Soviet Russia, Italy, and Germany are completely different, it must be said that their current success is due to proper leadership and effective use. The weak expression of popular power in China in recent years can be said to have reached its extreme. Taking the boycott of Japanese goods as an example, from an abstract point of view, it is of course something that the general public agrees with, but in practice, it is contrary to theory. Why? Because although boycotting Japanese goods is an idea that can be called upon, it is not effective due to the lack of leadership and application. Therefore, even an idea that can easily form power is just a name and cannot be achieved! We see that all problems in China today are not on track, and cannot produce a nationally unified force. In addition to the problem of the ideas themselves, the lack of people who lead ideas and methods of using ideas is indeed an important issue that deserves our attention.

The Goblins in Our Nation's Life 282

— Jie

If you pass by the gate of a certain postal administration office, you are sure to see a group of people gathered there looking like beggars, with disheveled hair and dirty faces, wearing tattered clothes, resembling a group of goblins released from the gates of hell. However, although you often see this group of goblins, you may never have paid attention to their lives. Don't underestimate this group of goblins; they are the most hardworking, enduring, healthy, and outstanding citizens of our nation, but their lives are forever below the poverty line. I have even seen several who froze to death in the snow on the steps and were taken away by charitable organizations for burial.

The reality is this: when the post office is busy, for example, when ocean liners arrive in or depart from Shanghai, there is a large amount of mail that needs to be transported. At this time, a batch of temporary laborers are hired outside the gate to carry the mail. In recent years, with frequent transportation and an increasing volume of mail, the demand for temporary laborers has been especially high, with about a hundred people needed every day. The working hours are not fixed, ranging from as short as one or two hours to as long as a full day, depending on the degree of business. Their compensation is calculated by the hour and paid in cash, at the rate of ten cents per hour. The post office, because of the low cost, is happy to entrust all the heavy labor to them. This is much cheaper than hiring a permanent workforce, and they can be summoned at will and dismissed at will. If there is work, they are paid to hire; if there is no work, they can be ignored, and there is no danger of strikes. Perhaps this is very much in line with the principles of scientific management!

China's industry is not thriving, and the countryside is frequently bankrupt. The number of unemployed people is increasing day by day. As a result, there are too many people waiting for work in front of the post office. Therefore, the temporary workers needed by the post office are also experiencing a phenomenon of oversupply, with more monks than gruel. If the post office needs to hire ten temporary laborers at a certain time, a postal worker stands in a high place, takes ten pieces of paper, and throws them to the ground, while the group of goblin-like coolies below compete with each other. Whoever is stronger and grabs a piece of paper can work for a few hours. The old and weak, of course, do not get a chance and can only hang their heads in frustration, watching others work. But the young and strong who grab a piece of paper are not necessarily able to make ends meet. If they manage to grab five hours of work each day, they can have food and a bunkhouse to live in, maintaining the bare minimum of daily life. But if they fail to grab any work one day, or only work for one or two hours, they can only go hungry and cold, sleeping in the corners of the alleys. Especially on Sundays and holidays, the post office is closed as usual, with no work available, but the stomach refuses to rest. Without food, one will starve. Therefore, during the Lunar New Year, the post office closed for four consecutive days, leaving them without work for four days, which simply put them to death. However, during this festive New Year, when young masters and their girlfriends are leisurely enjoying themselves, who will think of this group of goblins enduring hunger in the wind and snow? Yet, they are the most hardworking, enduring, and outstanding citizens of our nation!

A Discussion on Professions: The Standard of a Proper Profession 283

— Qiu

"(So-and-so) does not engage in a proper profession" is a common phrase used to criticize those who do not have so-called proper professions. But what can be considered a proper profession? In the minds of people today, there is no fixed standard. For example, the profession of being an official is not only regarded as a proper profession by people in society, but also as the most glorious and noble profession. However, upon careful examination, the mentality of many officials is simply to make money and improve their own lives and status. This not only cannot be considered a proper profession, but it cannot even be called a profession at all. As for general corrupt officials who specialize in plundering and exploiting others, it would be a great injustice to call this a proper profession!

If the explanation of a proper profession is said to be based on the individual, as long as he uses his physical and mental labor to earn compensation, it can be said that he is not living off the blood and sweat of others and therefore has a proper profession, then even the wandering performers in the lower classes are contributing their performance skills. The bodies of martial arts performers are bruised all over, yet they only earn a few coins. Isn't this using their physical and mental labor to earn compensation? Not only those wandering performers, but even prostitutes endure humiliation and sacrifice their bodies to earn a few coins to live on. Isn't this also a proper profession of using physical and mental labor to earn compensation? Yet, people say that the professions of wandering performers and prostitutes are not proper professions.

In this case, the evaluation of what constitutes a proper profession must have a standard. Otherwise, we cannot ask everyone to engage in proper professions. However, the standards for proper professions set in today's society are inappropriate because everyone is centered on the individual, believing that as long as a person can obtain personal satisfaction through the price of his labor, he has a proper profession. In fact, when we evaluate whether a certain profession is proper, we must consider whether it is beneficial to human beings and social progress, and whether it can become part of the division of labor in social production. We can call a profession that meets these two prerequisites a proper profession; otherwise, it cannot be considered a proper profession.

Because of this, we can easily distinguish which professions are proper and which are not; and even within the same profession, we can distinguish which are proper and which are not. For example, with regard to the profession of being an official, if we follow the above standards, not only is being a corrupt official not a proper profession, but also participating in any organization that hinders social progress and undertaking work that hinders social progress cannot be considered a proper profession. On the other hand, working hard in a social organization that can promote social progress and fulfilling its function of promoting social progress and social production development can be considered a proper profession. Workers engaged in production, doctors, professors, writers, and artists, as long as they stand on the side of progress and can promote society and its productive endeavors, can all be called those who undertake one of the proper divisions of labor. In this sense, the professions of wandering performers and prostitutes are, of course, improper. We hope that society can provide everyone with a proper profession, and we also hope that no one in society will be forced to engage in an improper profession.

A Small Monograph: The Reasons for Discrimination Against People of Color 284

— Ren

In southern Africa, in colonies ruled by self-proclaimed civilized imperialist nations, we can see many bizarre phenomena. Those white people who consider themselves to be a superior race spare no effort to slander and insult people of color: for example, when traveling, black people can only ride in segregated vehicles; they cannot enter schools or theaters; they do not even have the right to ride streetcars or walk on sidewalks because, in the eyes of white people, black people are simply not qualified to be called human beings.

In German criminal law, there is even a clause that states: (If a German citizen has physical relations with a person of color, the state considers this act to be treason against the race, and the parties involved in the marriage shall be punished.) In civil law, such marriages are invalid. In the eyes of German legislators, such marriages with people of color hinder the development of the superior race and violate the glory of the German nation because the whole reason is: in the eyes of the German people, these people of color are simply not qualified to be called human beings.

Why do white people have this kind of discrimination against people of color? There are several different answers to this question:

(1) This school of thought believes that the source of discrimination against people of color lies in the expression of the need for self-preservation of individuals and groups. Therefore, they oppose immigration by people of color and cooperation with people of color.

Page 23

(2) This school of thought believes that these behaviors all contain sexual connotations. They explained that white women like people of color, so white men feel a kind of jealousy, which is the origin of discrimination.

(3) This school of thought, on the one hand, expresses regret for the mutual hostility between races, but on the other hand, believes that superior races have the obligation to cultivate inferior races.

The first school of thought explains the interests of discriminating against people of color from the position of the imperialist children of the motherland. They explain that to consolidate and maintain the interests of capitalists and some white workers in their own country, it is necessary to cruelly exploit people of color. Based on this policy, they do their best to propagate rumors about the violence and incompetence of people of color. In Africa, the wages of black people are fifteen shillings a week, while those of white workers are eight pounds a week. However, since the outbreak of the world economic panic in 1929, both white and black people have been severely affected. The fate of black people is, of course, tragic, and there are many white unemployed people. They looked for work everywhere, but because of the low cost of black labor, there was terrible competition. White people were indeed under considerable threat, so they expanded the gap of discrimination between races. The British Labour Party is the party that represents the interests of these white workers. It implemented a resolution to prohibit black people from becoming standard workers. However, many white workers felt that they had the same tragic fate as black workers. The second school of thought attempts to explain this social phenomenon in terms of sexual relations, but this attempt is clearly a failure. Sex is, for example, a link in the chain, but not the main link. The main link is an economic relationship, and this economic foundation is what explains the importance of the superstructure. Let us now assume that the phenomenon of white women liking people of color exists, but at least we should not explain it in terms of sexual relations. We should explain it in terms of very complicated reasons, the main one of course being economic reasons. This reason is self-evident, because the number of white women marrying people of color is, after all, not large, and it is clearly impossible to cause the jealousy and resentment of white people.

The third school of thought believes that white people should raise the culture of people of color and that the level of culture is proportional to the amount of needs. Therefore, in order to increase their needs, they work hard to promote commodities. This argument is very contradictory because, as a result of commodity dumping, people of color inevitably go bankrupt. After bankruptcy, their low-cost labor poses a great threat to white people, which in turn causes hostility. Therefore, this argument cannot justify itself either.

Summarizing the above, we can know that the origin of this discrimination against people of color is nothing more than what is determined by the mode of production.

Commentary

Promoting National Goods and Revitalizing the Countryside 285

— Dong Wu

Everyone knows that China is a country based on agriculture. Farmers make up the largest majority of the national population, and the countryside is the largest place of consumption and production. If our agricultural production is very developed, and the products consumed in the countryside are all our own national goods, then our entire industry will inevitably develop, and the country's status will never be like it is today.

Unfortunately, however, our countryside is the vast raw material cultivation base of imperialism and the major market for dumping its goods. Under the control of the magic power of imperialism, our rural economy can neither preserve its old form nor embark on a new path, and it is inevitably falling into a crisis of bankruptcy. In recent years, as a result of various natural and man-made disasters, our rural economy has been completely bankrupt. The decline in agricultural productivity and the reduction in rural purchasing power are the real phenomena of the current Chinese countryside.

The decline in agricultural productivity has allowed imperialist agricultural products to be dumped into China in large quantities, in order to absorb our cash. The reduction in rural purchasing power has caused the industrial products of the cities to lose a vast market and cannot develop. This is one of the main reasons for the decline of Chinese industry and everything falling into poverty. People promote national goods, but they only see the cities and not the countryside. They only know that the sales of imperialist goods in the cities hinder the development of national goods, but they do not know that their foreign cloth, foreign oil, foreign rice, etc., also hinder the development of national goods when they are dumped into the countryside. Therefore, from last year's (National Goods Year) to this year's (Women's National Goods Year), whether it was (men) or (women), neither did a good job. As a result, all the silk factories in Shanghai went bankrupt together, a large number of silk weaving factories closed down, and foreign rice imports amounted to 16 to 17 million dan, with an excess of 80 to 90 million yuan!

I believe that if we don't talk about promoting national goods, then so be it. If we want to talk about promoting national goods, we must revitalize the rural economy. The meaning of promoting national goods should be and must be: to revitalize industry and agriculture and to prosper both cities and the countryside. If we leave the countryside alone and only stay in the cities to promote national goods, scolding fashionable women every day, there will be no future!

At the same time, and more importantly, we should actively rise up to remove the economic and political shackles of imperialism on us. If we do not do this and only avoid the substance and promote national goods, shouting what (changing people's hearts), there will be no future either. Because imperialism can not only use our tariff autonomy to dump its goods, but also open factories, mines, operate shipping, and establish concessions in our interior. Our entire economic life is held in the palms of imperialism. If we do not work hard to use active methods to desperately break out of its palms, and fantasize about growing and developing peacefully in its palms, aren't we dreaming?

Special Solicitation

The Mystery of Rationalizing Commissions 286

— Ci An

Last Sunday, we asked this publication to convey a message to unemployed friends to solicit a few advertising colleagues. The next day, we received more than a dozen applications, and letters continued to arrive on the third and fourth days.

At first, we only wanted to find a few friends to help, but Mr. Editor added a title of (Rationalizing Commissions) to the free advertisement in the last issue, which made many people want to understand. Even current employees of two advertising companies came to inquire. Of course, they were not here to apply, but to ask about the method.

Now, let's use this publication's filler space to provide an answer.

Most of the personnel who serve in the advertising departments of major newspapers are paid monthly salaries, just like the employees of other departments. In large-scale advertising companies, advertising staff also receive salaries, in addition to commissions. Next, there are only commissions and transportation expenses, without salaries. We can't even afford transportation expenses now, so we can only rely on commissions. Usually, commissions are handled uniformly, that is, 30% is 30%, and 20% is only 20%. Whether you work hard or not, it doesn't matter; in any case, a few percent is a few percent. There is no reward for pulling in more advertising.

We now stipulate that the percentage of commissions should increase with the amount of advertising, so that those who work hard will receive extra compensation. To put it simply: (1) When the total amount of advertising revenue handled by each person per month is less than 500 yuan, the commission is only 20%; (2) When it exceeds 500 yuan but is less than 1,000 yuan, the commission is calculated at 25%; (3) When it exceeds 1,000 yuan but is less than 2,000 yuan, the commission is 30%; (4) All amounts above 2,000 yuan are calculated at 35%. In addition, all advertising staff must sign a three-month trial contract upon entry. After three months, if both parties are satisfied, the period will be extended.

As of the time of writing, most of the letters we have received are from students who have just left or are about to leave school. However, we are deeply afraid that the students will not be used to this kind of advertising life because going out to find business requires asking for help from people at every step, relying on people, fawning on people, and may even be ridiculed by others in the end. However, we are still extremely welcome to the students, as long as individuals have the courage, perseverance, and the ability to deal with wealthy people or arrogant big shots, they will certainly be able to do the job happily. Otherwise, although the newspaper can take care of food and lodging, we also think it is a pity to waste the time of young people.

If there are still friends who want to try, feel free to write to us as before to discuss it because we do need advertising staff.

Please send letters directly to the Advertising Department of the Citizen Newspaper, Taipingfang, Hankou Road, and do not ask Mr. Di to forward them, to avoid additional procedures.

Glamorous Shanghai

Cross-section of Nanjing Road 287

— Pu Lin

Nanjing Road! The heart of this great Shanghai!

Here, the rocky cliffs of buildings form a deep riverbed, where streams of people, vehicles, and money are intertwined. From east to west, from south to north, the giant streams flow continuously. They constantly impact the great city, the great civilization, and the great era.

Atop the seven-story buildings, steel-boned spires soar, reflecting red and green lights like electric torches, and the radio plays the symphony of the metropolis—Xuangong's love history, commercial reports, Mei Lanfang, political news, Wang Wuneng, Ding Guaiguai.

Banners for big sales flutter everywhere—big sales, bargain sales, dumping, big XXX. From the ground to the roof, from the roof to the sky, the banners of big sales stretch out their giant hands, seizing everyone's heart and the first person's money.

Nanjing Road! Here, people are flying, vehicles are flying, money is flying, and time is flying too.

In that great department store, the bridge of cigarettes faces the mountain of thermos bottles, and the harbor of coats is surrounded by the sea of silks; Miss’s head is buried in a pile of socks, choosing silk stockings with floral heels; young wives are in the aisle of cosmetics, picking out the lipstick they need; children are throwing tantrums at their grandmothers, insisting on buying the lopsided Chaplin; newlyweds lean on their husbands' shoulders, considering children's clothing; in the corner, two art school students are arguing over the patterns on the carpet; ...hubbub, quarrels, bells, laughter, shoe sounds, coughs.

Elevators are constantly devouring and spewing, extending all the way to the night garden on the roof. The stage of life, the theater of joys and sorrows, the dance of the times.

A transaction began in the corner: (Hey! Young master! Going home to play?)

(Where is your home?) (········) (········) Three rickshaws sped past the New World five minutes later.

In the Hongmiao Temple, devout men and women are bowing and kowtowing, and the incense is like the chimneys of the industrial district, drifting and pervading. As soon as the elder sister enters this temple surrounded by cement and steel, she prays very piously, asking the Bodhisattva to give her a dream of revelation so that she can win this round of lotteries.

Outside the temple: (Want one! Fountain pen!...) Then, the tram stopped in the center of Zhejiang Road intersection, and several voices immediately surrounded the tram: (Hey! Da Mei Evening News, Da Wan Night News...) (Hey! 130,000 yuan fraud case! Hey!) Thirteen-year-old girl giving birth, hey...)
